Translation

d. тМК4.тМЛ of
both the bс╣Ыh├бt and the rathaс╣Бtar├б and of the ─Аdityas and of all the
gods doth he become the dear abode (dh─Б╠Бman) [who knoweth thus]. Of
him in the eastern quarter

Notes

The natural division of the matter of this and the following verses is
in the latter half strangely violated by the tradition. Division d
should most certainly have at its end y├б ev├бс╣Б v├йda, as is shown by the
requirements of the sense and by the occurrence of these words in the
same connection in 6. 1-9, 8. 3, and 9. 3; but the phrase is wanting in
all the mss.; we have introduced it in our text, and the translation
gives it (in brackets). Then the mss. most senselessly reckon to d
the words which really introduce e-h, or the second half of the
verse; i.e., they set no avas─Бna before t├бsya, but have one after
di┼Ы├н; and the Anukr. follows the same method; it is corrected in our
text тМКalthough the division by letters in the translation follows the
mss.тМЛ; the analogy of the verses of hymns 4 and 5 is a sufficient
justification for so doing. In the second half, the only natural
division is after puraс╕еsar─Б├║; very strangely, however, the mss. and
Anukr. set no avas─Бna here, but one, altogether out of place, after
pratod├бs, and two that are uncalled for after maс╣З├нs and vipath├бm
respectively; of these two we have retained only that after maс╣З├нs (as
it denoted a certain change of subject), while we have shifted forward
to its proper place the one after pratod├бs. The metrical definitions
of the Anukr. are evidently applicable, with the usual degree of
exactness, to the divisions as made by the mss.

The translation follows the mss. in reading in e mitr├│ (but all
save Bs.s.m.D.R. accent m├нtro) m─Бgadh├│. тМКCorrect the Berlin ed. from
m├бntro to mitr├│.тМЛ The Pet. Lex. conjectures pravarta to signify a
rounded ornament. тМКAs for turban, goad, etc., see p. 770, ┬╢ 2.тМЛ тМКPpp.
has sa pr─Бc─лс╣Б di┼Ыam anuvyacalat; the remainder of the book is
wanting.тМЛ

Griffith

He who hath this knowledge becomes the beloved home of the Brihat, the Rathantara the Adityas, and all the Gods.

Griffith

In the eastern region Faith is his leman, the hymn his panegyrist, knowledge his vesture, day his turban, night his hair, Indra’s two Bays his circular ornaments, the splendour of the stars his jewel.
